## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration in such systems is governed by restoring forces (functions of x) and damping forces (functions of v), potentially with nonlinear terms like cubic restoring forces (Duffing oscillator) or nonlinear damping.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (polynomial damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**2 * v + c3 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v**2 (full polynomial expansion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force → term proportional to -x (simple harmonic behavior)
- Cubic position dependence → x**3 term indicates Duffing-type hardening or softening nonlinearity
- Position-dependent damping → v * x**2 or v * (1 - x**2) terms indicate Van der Pol-type self-excitation
- Odd-power restoring forces → x, x**3, x**5 preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium
- Nonlinear damping → v**3 or v*abs(v) terms model amplitude-dependent energy dissipation
- Periodic external forcing → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms indicate driven oscillator dynamics
- Asymmetric potential → even powers of x (x**2) break the symmetry and shift equilibrium
- Limit cycle behavior → combination of negative linear damping and positive nonlinear damping (c1*v + c2*v**3 with opposite signs)

Expanding: `0.194830767863936*v*x**2 - 0.194830767863936*v - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-|x|) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v*x²` (coefficient ≈ 0.1948)
2. `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.1948)
3. `x*exp(-|x|)` (coefficient ≈ -3.049)
4. `sin(v)` (coefficient ≈ -0.143)

Key observations:
- The term `x*exp(-|x|)` is a specific function that cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, tanh, sin(x), etc.
- `sin(v)` is a function of v, distinct from `sin(x)`

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these exact basis functions.

**The critical question is whether any candidate can produce `x*exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)` exactly.**

For `x*exp(-|x|)`: No polynomial, tanh, sin, log, or simple algebraic combination can exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x. The function `tanh(c1*x)` approaches ±1 for large |x| while `x*exp(-|x|)` approaches 0, so they're fundamentally different.

For `sin(v)`: Only candidates with `sin(v)` or `sin(c*v)` (with c=1) can match this.

Let me check which candidates have `sin(v)`:
- **Candidate 20**: has `sin(c3*v)` ✓ and `sin(c5*x)` and `tanh(c1*x)` — but still needs `x*exp(-|x|)` which can't be made from tanh + sin(x)
- **Candidate 21**: has `tanh(c7*v)` not sin(v)

None of the candidates contain `x*exp(-|x|)` or any equivalent. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is not a polynomial, not tanh, not sin, not log. It's a unique transcendental function.

Let me verify: Could `tanh(c1*x) + sin(c3*x) + c6*x` somehow equal `x*exp(-|x|)`? No — tanh is bounded, sin is periodic, and x is unbounded. Their sum cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)` which decays to 0.

Could `x**c3 + x**c5` work? Power functions don't have exponential decay.

Could `x*sin(c4 + c5*x)` work? No, it oscillates.

Could `x*exp(c7*x)` (Candidate 44) work? For x > 0, we need `exp(-x)`, so c7 = -1. For x < 0, we need `exp(x)`, so c7 = 1. Can't have both — this fails because `exp(-|x|)` is not `exp(c*x)`.

No candidate can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` since none contain `exp(-|x|)` or `Abs(x)` in an exponential.

Therefore, **no candidate matches the GT**.
